SETTLEMENT AGREEMENT
Transmitting a Communication from
TODD H. STROGER, President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
respectfully transmitting a request for approval of a settlement agreement between the County and the
Village of Rosemont (“Village”) regarding County of Cook v. Village of Rosemont, Case No. 97-L50281 (the Amusement Tax litigation).

5544

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
Pursuant to the terms of the settlement agreement, the Village will pay the County $4,276,876.00 on or
before May 9, 2008 in exchange for the County’s dismissal of the Amusement Tax Lawsuit and will also
provide certain maintenance and police patrol services to the District for a ten-year period beginning on
June 1, 2008. These services will be provided pursuant to the terms of an intergovernmental agreement
between the Village and the Forest Preserve District of Cook County, which is an exhibit to the settlement
agreement.
The Litigation Subcommittee has approved the terms and conditions of this proposed settlement.
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the request of the President be
approved and that the Proper Officials be authorized to sign on behalf of Cook County. The motion
carried unanimously.
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance Amendment sponsored by
TODD H. STROGER, President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that Chapter 2 Administration,
Article IV Officers and Employees, Division 3 Recorder of Deeds, Subsection II Fees, Section 2-214 GIS
fee and Chapter 32 Fees, Section 32-1 fee schedule, of the Cook County Code are hereby amended as
follows:
Sec. 2-214.
(a)

GIS Fee.
The terms used in this section shall have the meanings set forth below:

Additional charge is a charge as set out in Section 32-1, which is added to the existing fees
imposed by the County Recorder for the filing of every instrument, paper, or notice of record.
Countywide map is a parcel based map of the County which includes all the supporting
Geographic Information System.
Geographic information system is an organized collection of computer hardware, software, and
geographic data designed to efficiently capture, store, update, manipulate, analyze, and display all forms
of geographically referenced information.
(b)

The charge will be distributed as follows:
(1)

Fourteen Twelve dollars will be deposited into a distinct fund set up by the
County Bureau of Information Technology and Automation. These monies will
be used solely to finance equipment, materials, and other necessary expenses
incurred in implementing and maintaining a geographic information system.

(2)

One Three dollars will be deposited by the Recorder pursuant to 55ILCS 5/35005.4 (deposit of fee income-special funds).

RESOLUTIONS
08-R-104
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER, PRESIDENT, WILLIAM M. BEAVERS,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE QUIGLEY, TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
ROBERT B. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Cook County fosters intergovernmental cooperation among its many member
municipalities, townships and other local governments and organizations in the State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the City of Chicago has been selected by the United States Olympic Committee as the U.S.
Applicant City for the international competition to host the 2016 Olympic and Paralympic Games; and
WHEREAS, the City and the other municipalities in the metropolitan Chicago region are anxious to
serve the Olympic Movement by embracing and celebrating the Olympic Games; and
WHEREAS, the Olympic and Paralympic Games represent the best of the human spirit, and Chicago
2016 and the United States Olympic Committee are committed to bringing the 2016 Olympics and
Paralympic Games to the United States for the benefit of all and to inspire harmony locally, nationally
and globally; and
WHEREAS, Chicago, a world-class city with remarkable diversity, culture, history and people, already
holds a place in the international community as a city and a metropolitan area of immigrants from around
the world who are eager to be ambassadors to visiting Olympic athletes; and

5546

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, hosting the Games in the heartland of the country will provide a unique opportunity to
enhance the development of Olympic sport in the Midwest and across the nation; and
WHEREAS, the Olympic and Paralympic Games in Chicago would provide a spectacular experience for
athletes, the Olympic Family, spectators, residents and the global viewing audience by celebrating the
Games in the center of the City and throughout the metropolitan region and in the midst of millions of
people who are passionate about sports, and will create an energetic spirit inside and outside of the
venues; and
WHEREAS, Chicago is one of the transportation hubs of the world and can provide accessible
transportation to international visitors through its extensive rail, transit and motorways infrastructure,
combined with world-class international airports.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that Cook County supports the City of Chicago and
Chicago 2016 as they compete for the privilege to host the 2016 Olympic and Paralympic Games; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that Cook County pledges its assistance to enhance the efforts of the
City and Chicago 2016 to host the 2016 Olympic and Paralympic Games; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that Cook County respectfully encourages its member municipalities,
townships and other local governments and organizations to support the City of Chicago and Chicago
2016 as they compete for the privilege of hosting the 2016 Olympic and Paralympic Games.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, ROBERT B. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

5547

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
PUBLIC HEALTH WEEK 2008
WHEREAS, the Cook County Department of Public Health is concerned about the impact that climate
change has on the health of our residents; and
WHEREAS, most Americans, including the public health workforce, remain largely unprepared for
public health challenges associated with climate change; and
WHEREAS, the nation’s most vulnerable populations, including young children, the elderly, and those
suffering from chronic illnesses, and people in underserved communities, are most likely to be
disproportionately impacted yet least able to prepare, respond and recover from the health effects of
climate change; and
WHEREAS, in suburban Cook County, extreme weather, such as freezing temperatures and heat waves
have caused death and illness among the elderly; and
WHEREAS, vector borne disease, such as West Nile virus, sickened hundreds of people and caused
dozens of deaths in suburban Cook County in 2002 and is related to climate conditions that allow
mosquitoes to breed; and
WHEREAS, local, state and federal governments along with numerous other organizations must increase
efforts to educate Americans and the public health workforce about what they need to do to mitigate and
adapt to the consequences of climate change; and
WHEREAS, all communities must plan in advance to ensure their residents are prepared for and can
respond to the health consequences of climate change.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that I, Todd H. Stroger, President of the Cook County
Board of Commissioners, declare April 7-13, 2008 as Public Health Week in Cook County, and

commend this observance to all our residents.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

08-R-106
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER, PRESIDENT AND WILLIAM M. BEAVERS,
JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE QUIGLEY, TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
ROBERT B. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Almighty God in His Infinite Wisdom has called a champion for political justice and one of
the most brilliant legal minds of the past 100 years, Judge R. Eugene Pincham, from our midst; and
WHEREAS, Judge Pincham was raised by his mother in Alabama, where he overcame segregation,
racism and extreme poverty to rise to become one of the standard bearers of the civil rights movement;
and
WHEREAS, Judge Pincham attended Trinity School in Athens, Alabama, a grammar and high school
founded in 1866 by an abolitionist organization, the American Missionary Association, to educate the
newly emancipated slaves; and
WHEREAS, Judge Pincham earned a bachelor’s degree in 1947 from Tennessee State University, where
he was initiated into Kappa Alpha Psi Fraternity and was president of the Tennessee State University
Student Council for the 1946-1947 term; Judge Pincham earned a law degree as one of only two African
Americans in the Northwestern Law School Class of 1951; he worked as a waiter in the Palmer House
Hotel on weeknights and shined shoes on the weekends to finance his law school education; and
WHEREAS, in the summer of 1951 Judge Pincham began his practice of law as a trial and appeals
attorney, in criminal and civil litigation; he became a partner in the law firm of Evans, Pincham, Fowlkes
& Cooper, and was admitted to the Bar of the Supreme Court of the United States in 1965; as a defense
attorney, Judge Pincham was one of the most brilliant and impassioned orators of his day; he used his
superb oratory skills to fight for justice for the disenfranchised; and
WHEREAS, Judge Pincham served as a Circuit Court Judge in the Criminal Division from 1976 to 1984
and as an Illinois Appellate Judge from 1984 to 1990; during his tenure as a judge he authored thousands
of opinions and successfully appealed over 200 cases; he was known for writing dissenting opinions
while on the Appellate Court, many of which were later adopted as majority opinions; and
WHEREAS, Judge Pincham was not afraid of controversy and used his station to speak out on behalf of
justice regardless of whether his position was popular or not; he was a vocal and grounded critic of the
police and the courts and worked doggedly for the political advancement of African Americans; and
WHEREAS, because the Illinois Judicial Canon of Ethics prohibited a sitting judge from seeking a nonjudicial elective office, Judge Pincham resigned from the Appellate Court in 1990 to seek the Democratic
Party nomination for President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners in the March 1990 primary
election; and

5549

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, after retiring from the bench, Judge Pincham continued to practice law, and lectured at
Harvard University, as well as at the University of Chicago, Northwestern University, Notre Dame
University and DePaul University; and
WHEREAS, Judge Pincham was preceded in death by his devoted wife of 53 years, Alzata; and is
survived by two sons, Robert and James, a daughter, Andrea, and two grandchildren; his memory shall be
cherished in their hearts and in all of the hearts of the people whom he loved and whose lives he touched.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf
of the more than five million residents of Cook County, hereby does express its deepest condolences and
most heartfelt sympathy to the family as well as to the many friends and loved ones of Judge R. Eugene
Pincham.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

PRESENTATION
The following item was deferred at the March 6, 2008 Board Meeting:
Transmitting a Communication, dated February 25, 2008 from
MIKE QUIGLEY, County Commissioner
this request formally invites the Assessor’s Office to give a presentation highlighting the newest website
features available on the Assessor’s website. We appreciate all of the efforts the Assessor’s office has
made to comply with the amended Cook County Ethics Ordinance. The amendments to the Ethics
Ordinance sought to bring a greater level of transparency to the property tax appeal process, and the
changes made to the Assessor’s website have facilitated this goal of increased transparency. The recent
advancements to the Assessor’s website, making all property tax appeals data available and easily
accessible to the public, demonstrate the office’s willingness to go above and beyond our expectations of
transparency and equality in the tax appeal process.

5550

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
In an effort to share the Assessor’s latest achievement with all Cook County Board members, county
employees, the press, and anyone who might utilize this new feature, we hope they will be available to
present the new website features at a Cook County Board meeting.
_________________________
This item was WITHDRAWN at the request of the sponsor.
PROPOSED ORDINANCES
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
An Ordinance providing for voter input with regards to any future Cook
County tax increases which exceed the rate of inflation or consumer price
index (CPI) adjustments.
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a Home Rule unit and may, under the power granted by Section 6(a)
of Article VII of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois, exercise any power and perform any
function pertaining to its government and affairs, including, but not limited to, the power to tax and to
incur debt; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board has recently voted to impose a $500 million tax increase upon the
residents of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the amount of this tax increase is equal to roughly twice the amount of the actual county
deficit; and
WHEREAS, this tax increase will result in Cook County having a sales tax of more than 10%, which will
result in many residents fleeing to other counties to make purchases; and
WHEREAS, the decision of whether to increase taxes by such a dramatic amount should be made by the
voters of Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, Illinois, as follows:
ARTICLE I. DEFINITIONS
(a)

Ballot issue means a non-recall petition or referred measure in an election.

(b)

County means any the County of Cook, and includes any and all entities of the County of

Cook.
(c)
Fiscal year spending means all county expenditures and reserve increases except, as to
both, those for refunds made in the current or next fiscal year or those from gifts, federal funds,
collections for another government, pension contributions by employees and pension fund earnings,
reserve transfers or expenditures, damage awards, or property sales.

5551

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
(d)
Inflation means the percentage change in the United States Bureau of Labor Statistics
Consumer Price Index for Cook County, all items, all urban consumers, or its successor index.
(e)
Local growth for the county means a net percentage change in actual value of all real
property in Cook County from construction of taxable real property improvements, minus destruction of
similar improvements, and additions to, minus deletions from, taxable real property.
ARTICLE II. SPENDING LIMITS
(a)
The maximum annual percentage change in the county’s fiscal year spending equals
inflation in the prior calendar year plus annual local growth, adjusted for revenue changes approved by
voters.
(b)
The maximum annual percentage change in the county’s property tax revenue equals
inflation in the prior calendar year plus annual local growth, adjusted for property tax revenue changes
approved by voters.
(c)
If revenue from sources not excluded from fiscal year spending exceeds these limits in
dollars for that fiscal year, the excess shall be refunded in the next fiscal year unless voters approve a
revenue change as an offset. Initial bases are current fiscal year spending and property tax collected in
that year. Qualification or disqualification as an enterprise shall change bases and future year limits.
Future creation of bonded debt shall increase, and retiring or refinancing county bonded debt shall lower,
fiscal year spending and property tax revenue by the annual debt service so funded. Debt service changes,
reductions, refunds, and voter-approved revenue changes are dollar amounts that are exceptions to, and
not part of, any county base. Voter-approved revenue changes do not require a tax rate change.
ARTICLE III. EMERGENCY PROVISIONS
(a)
Emergency reserves. To use for declared emergencies only, the county shall reserve 3%
of its fiscal year spending excluding bonded debt service. Unused reserves apply to the next year’s
reserve.
(b)
Emergency taxes. This subsection grants no new taxing power. Emergency property taxes
are prohibited. Emergency taxes shall also meet the following conditions: a 2/3 majority of the members
of the county board declares the emergency and imposes the tax by separate recorded roll call votes.
(c)
Emergency tax revenue shall be spent only after emergency reserves are depleted, and
shall be refunded within 180 days after the emergency ends if not spent on the emergency.
(d)
A tax not approved on the next election date 60 days or more after the declaration shall
end with that election month.
ARTICLE IV. ELECTION PROVISIONS
(a)

Effective immediately upon passage, the county must have voter approval in advance for:
(i)

Any new tax, tax rate increase, mill levy above that for the prior year, valuation
for assessment ratio increase for a property class, or extension of an expiring tax,
or a tax policy change directly causing a net tax revenue gain to the county.

5552

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
(ii)

Except for refinancing county bonded debt at a lower interest rate or adding new
employees to existing district pension plans, creation of any multiple-fiscal year
direct or indirect county debt or other financial obligation whatsoever without
adequate present cash reserves pledged irrevocably and held for payments in all
future fiscal years.

(b)
Ballot issues shall be decided in a county-wide election. Except for petitions, bonded
debt, or charter or constitutional provisions, the county may consolidate ballot issues and voters may
approve a delay of up to four years in voting on ballot issues. District actions taken during such a delay
shall not extend beyond that period.
(c)
At least 30 days before a ballot issue election, the county shall mail at the least cost, a
titled notice or set of notices addressed to “All Registered Voters” at each address of one or more active
registered electors. Titles shall have this order of preference: “NOTICE OF ELECTION TO
INCREASE TAXES/TO INCREASE DEBT/ON A CITIZEN PETITION/ON A REFERRED
MEASURE.” Except for district voter-approved additions, notices shall include only:
(i)

The election date, hours, ballot title, text, and local election office address and
telephone number.

(ii)

For proposed county tax or bonded debt increases, the estimated or actual total of
county fiscal year spending for the current year and each of the past four years,
and the overall percentage and dollar change.

(iii)

For the first full fiscal year of each proposed county tax increase, county
estimates of the maximum dollar amount of each increase and of county fiscal
year spending without the increase.

(iv)

For proposed county bonded debt, its principal amount and maximum annual and
total repayment cost, and the principal balance of total current county bonded
debt and its maximum annual and remaining total repayment cost.

(v)

Two summaries, up to 500 words each, one for and one against the proposal, of
written comments filed with the Cook County Clerk by 45 days before the
election. No summary shall mention names of persons or private groups, nor any
endorsements of or resolutions against the proposal. Petition representatives
following these rules shall write this summary for their petition. The county clerk
officer shall maintain and accurately summarize all other relevant written
comments.

(d)
Except by later voter approval, if a tax increase or fiscal year spending exceeds any
estimate in (b) (iii) for the same fiscal year, the tax increase is thereafter reduced up to 100% in
proportion to the combined dollar excess, and the combined excess revenue refunded in the next fiscal
year. County bonded debt shall not issue on terms that could exceed its share of its maximum repayment
costs in (b) (iv). Ballot titles for tax or bonded debt increases shall begin, “SHALL COOK COUNTY
TAXES BE INCREASED (first, or if phased in, final, full fiscal year dollar increase)
ANNUALLY...?” or “SHALL COOK COUNTY DEBT BE INCREASED (principal amount),
WITH A REPAYMENT COST OF (maximum total county cost), ...?”

5553

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
ARTICLE V. GENERAL PROVISIONS
(a)

This section takes effect immediately upon passage.

(b)
Other limits on county revenue, spending, and debt may be weakened only by future
voter approval.
(c)
Subject to judicial review, the county may use any reasonable method for refunds under
this section, including temporary tax credits or rate reductions. Refunds need not be proportional when
prior payments are impractical to identify or return.
(d)
When annual county revenue is less than annual payments on general obligation bonds,
pensions, and final court judgments, (4) (a) and (7) shall be suspended to provide for the deficiency.

PROPOSED ORDINANCE
PURSUANT TO THE HOME RULE AUTHORITY OF THE COUNTY OF COOK AS VESTED
IN IT BY THE ILLINOIS CONSTITUTION is hereby enacted the following Ordinance:
When a document is returned to the customer by the U.S. Postal Service, the Recorder of Deeds is hereby
authorized to charge, in addition to the recording fees, postage and handling fee of $2.25. The Recorder
of Deeds is authorized to modify the postage rate to reflect increases by the U.S. Postal Service.
The Recorder of Deeds is further authorized to rent mail type boxes to customers for delivery of
documents from the Recorder of Deeds Office. The Rental for each box shall be $20.00 per month.
This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect 30 days after passage by the Board of County
Commissioners.

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
ROBERT B. STEELE, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
RECORDER INTERNET DOCUMENT COPY FEE ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, pursuant to Counties Code, Fees 55 ILCS 5/3-5018 and Public records; Internet Access 55
ILCS 5/5 – 1106.1, the Recorder has been expressly authorized to charge a fee for obtaining documents
on the Internet for the purpose of offsetting the expense of providing such access; and
WHEREAS, Cook County is a “home rule” unit of local government, pursuant to Article VII, section
6(a) of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such, may exercise any power and perform any function
pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the Counties Code, Fees of Recorder in Third Class Counties, 55 ILCS 5/4- 12002, as
amended by P.A. 93-671 effective June 1, 2004 authorizes the Recorder to charge a fee for providing noncertified copies of documents in an amount of up to one half the fee charged for providing certified
copies; and
WHEREAS, on September 21, 2004, the Recorder Internet Document Fee Ordinance was passed,
providing a $.50 fee for an internet copy; and
WHEREAS, the Industrial Engineers surveyed the recording process and performed a cost analysis.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, for electronic copies of recorded documents obtained from
the Recorder’s Internet Website, the Recorder is hereby authorized to charge $1.50 per document.
This Ordinance shall be effective on passage.

PROPOSED RESOLUTIONS
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
A REFERENDUM ON HOME RULE
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a Home Rule unit and may, under the power granted by Section 6(a)
of Article VII of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois, exercise any power and perform any
function pertaining to its government and affairs, including, but not limited to, the power to tax and incur
debt; and

5555

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, this Home Rule power enables the Cook County Board President and Commissioners to
impose new and higher taxes on residents and taxpayers without the approval of Cook County voters; and
WHEREAS, Cook County is the only county in the State of Illinois that is Home Rule; and
WHEREAS, the voters of Cook County have never weighed in on the issue of Home Rule; and
WHEREAS, under Section 6(b) of Article VII of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois, a Home
Rule unit may, by referendum, elect not to be a Home Rule unit; and
WHEREAS, the voters of Cook County should be permitted to voice their opinion as to whether the
County of Cook shall remain a Home Rule unit; and
WHEREAS, it is deemed to be in the public interest to submit this question of policy to the voters of
Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED THAT:
Section 1. The following question of public policy shall be presented to the voters of Cook County as a
referendum at the general election scheduled for Tuesday, November 4, 2008, consistent with the Illinois
Elections Code; to wit;
“Shall the County of Cook continue to be a Home Rule unit of government?”
Section 2. This Referendum shall be conducted in accordance with provisions of the Illinois Election
Code pertaining to the conduct of the general election scheduled for November 4, 2008.
Section 3. This Resolution shall be in full force and effect upon its passage and approval.
_________________________
Commissioner Peraica, seconded by Commissioner Beavers, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
approved and adopted. Commissioner Peraica called for a Roll Call, the votes of yeas and nays being as
follows:
ROLL CALL ON THE MOTION TO APPROVE THE PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Yeas:

Peraica - 1.

Nays:

Beavers, Claypool, Collins, Daley, Maldonado, Moreno, Murphy, Schneider, Silvestri, Sims,
Steele, Suffredin - 12.

Absent:

Butler, Gorman, Goslin, Quigley - 4.

The motion to approve FAILED.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, WILLIAM M. BEAVERS, GREGG GOSLIN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, DEBORAH SIMS, ROBERT B. STEELE and
ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
RESOLUTION CONCERNING REMOVAL OF THE PUBLIC DEFENDER
WHEREAS, the office of the public defender is an office created by state statute, all as set forth in
Article 3, Division 3-4 of the Counties Code, 55 ILCS 5/1-1001, et seq. (“Illinois Law”); and
WHEREAS, Illinois Law sets forth the purpose of the public defender and the declaration of the General
Assembly of the State of Illinois wherein the General Assembly recognizes the People of the State of
Illinois’ fundamental right to quality legal representation in criminal and related proceedings; and
WHEREAS, Illinois Law also provides the process for appointment, the terms of employment, the oath
of office, the duties, the compensation, a provision for appointment of assistants, provisions for office
quarters and expenses and record keeping of the Public Defender in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners (the “President”) and the Cook
County Board of Commissioners clearly recognized the intent of the General Assembly to provide quality
legal representation to the indigent by seeking to reduce Edwin A. Burnette’s (hereinafter referred to as
the “Public Defender”) caseload by creating twenty-eight (28) new positions in the 2008 Budget; and

5557

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, notwithstanding the President’s and the Cook County Board of Commissioner’s willingness
to create twenty-eight (28) new positions to further ensure quality legal representation of the indigent,
during the Public Defender’s tenure, there were thirty-four (34) inmates of Cook County Jail (persons
held in custody who have not been convicted of a crime) who waited for trial for over five (5) years at an
approximate cost to the Cook County taxpayers of $5,584,500 ($90 per day for 34 inmates for 5 years),
while the Public Defender continues to fail to ensure that all assistant public defenders work a full forty
(40) hour work week, (See, Evaluation of the Juvenile Justice Division of the law office of the Cook
County Public Defender submitted herewith as Exhibit A on page 10 and hereinafter referred to as the
“Northwestern Report”); and
WHEREAS, Illinois Law provides the process for removing the Cook County Public Defender and is set
forth below:
The public defender once approved by the Board shall serve for 6 years and may be
removed by the President only for good cause or dereliction of duty after notice and a
hearing before the Board.
55 ILCS 5/3-4004.2(c) (emphasis added); and
WHEREAS, Black’s Law Dictionary defines dereliction in the performance of duties as:
[W]illful or negligent failure to perform assigned duties; culpable inefficiency in performing
assigned duties.
West Group, Black’s Law Dictionary 454 (7th ed. 2001); and
WHEREAS, the President, being the duly elected officer, has determined that there is good cause to
remove the Public Defender; and
WHEREAS, the Public Defender has willfully or negligently failed to perform the following assigned
duties as the Cook County Public Defender in that:
1.

The Public Defender failed to notify the administration of the Chicago Community
Group’s ongoing report concerning the Criminal Courts; and the Public Defender, as
cited in the Northwestern Report, failed to ensure that all employees of his office
performed a full forty (40) hour week of work in exchange for their compensation;
specifically, the Northwestern Report stated there existed a problem in his office
concerning the early departure of assistants after court (See, Exhibit A, page 10);

2.

The Public Defender has failed to timely process promotions of employees within his
office resulting in an unnecessary and unreasonable delay in the hiring of entry-level
employees. The following are examples of such failures:
•

On or about October 25, 2007, the Public Defender was provided with lists of
applicants for the promotional position of public defender III and IV. The Public
Defender has approximately fifteen (15) of these positions vacant. Filling these
positions would allow the Public Defender to create vacancies for public defender I
positions, and hire attorneys to reduce caseloads. As of March 31, 2008, the Public
Defender has failed to fill all such positions except three (3).

5558

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
•

In or about July, 2007, the Public Defender requested that five (5) public defender I
positions be reclassified to clerical positions within his office, further reducing his
ability to hire attorneys to reduce caseloads. This request was processed on or about
July 17, 2007.

•

Beginning on or about November 29, 2007, the Public Defender was advised that
supervisory positions could not be posted until job descriptions for those positions
were completed by his office and reviewed by the Bureau of Human Resources.
Despite repeated communications, these descriptions were not completed until midMarch, 2008. At about that same time, the Public Defender requested that these
positions not be posted, thereby placing the entire process in indefinite limbo.

Such failures have led this Public Defender to have a caseload greater than the national
standard. (See, Exhibit B submitted herewith the American Council of Chief Defenders
Statement on Caseloads and Workloads, August 24, 2007); and
3.

The Public Defender failed to ensure that all non-union employees complied with the
President’s executive order concerning the five (5) furlough day mandate, which
contributed to additional financial burden to Cook County and such savings should have
been reprogrammed back into services to the poor; and

4.

The Public Defender did not adequately handle the disciplinary issue of an employee
under his supervision who is alleged to have committed a crime in the workplace and
alleged to have been in possession of illegal and illicit drugs in the workplace; (See,
Exhibit C submitted herewith Pot Delivered to Public Defender’s Office Gets Clerk,
November 28, 2007); and

5.

The Public Defender has failed to identify Shakman Exempt positions as required under
the provisions of the Supplemental Relief Order and Consent Decree established in the 69
C 2145 and titled Shakman, et al v. The Democratic Organization, et al.; and

6.

The Public Defender misled the Cook County Board of Commissioners by seeking the
appointment of a Special State’s Attorney to provide “analysis, interpretation and advice”
(See, Exhibit D submitted herewith Petition for Appointment of a Special State’s
Attorney) and the Public Defender exceeded such authority granted to him by this Board
of Commissioners by suing the President thereby causing a potential financial liability to
the Cook County taxpayers to pay attorney fees to the Public Defender’s attorney and the
President’s attorney. (See, Exhibit E submitted herewith Public Defender’s Complaint
and See also, Exhibit F submitted herewith Motion to Dismiss Pursuant to Section 2619); and

WHEREAS, the President, after affording the Public Defender the right to a hearing before the Cook
County Board of Commissioners, should remove the Public Defender as the Public Defender of Cook
County if there exists good cause for such removal.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the
above stated recitals and whereas clauses are incorporated herein by reference; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that this Board of
Commissioners hereby finds that a hearing occurred to discuss whether the Public Defender was in fact
derelict in his duty and whether there is good cause for removal; and
5559

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that this Board of
Commissioners hereby supports the President’s removal of the Public Defender as the Public Defender of
Cook County in accordance with 55 ILCS 5/3-4004.2(c) for reasons set forth in this Resolution and at his
hearing before the President and this Board of Commissioners and further finds that his removal and the
appointment of another individual will best provide an environment where the taxpayers of Cook County
have greater confidence that resources allotted to the Cook County Public Defender are administered so
as to best fulfill his statutory duty to provide quality legal representation to the indigent of Cook County.
_________________________
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved to defer consideration of the Proposed
Resolution to the May 7, 2008 Board meeting. The motion carried unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ROBERTO MALDONADO, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, on April 2, 2008, SSM Health Care (SSM), one of the nation’s largest Catholic health care
systems, will close St. Francis Hospital & Health Center, situated on 14 acres at Western Avenue and
127th Street, after 103 years of serving the Blue Island community; and
WHEREAS, St. Francis is a non-profit, 410-bed acute-care hospital providing primary, secondary and
tertiary levels of care and offers a comprehensive range of medical, surgical, pediatric and obstetrical care
and services as well as cutting edge prevention and treatment of heart disease; and
WHEREAS, over the last seven years, SSM invested more than $75 million to modernize St. Francis into
a competitive, state-of-the-art facility that included an expanded emergency department, comprehensive
imaging and diagnostic services, outpatient surgery services, a women’s wellness center, a newly
dedicated endoscopy unit, and an award-winning cardiovascular center; and
WHEREAS, despite this investment, the hospital lost $40 million since 2002 and was projected to lose
$20 million in 2008 alone; and
WHEREAS, fifty percent of the people who come to St. Francis’ Emergency Department and twenty five
percent of the people who are admitted to the hospital either have no health insurance or are covered by
Medicaid; and
WHEREAS, state and federal reimbursements for Medicare and Medicaid have significantly slowed,
including $1.8 billion in unpaid Medicaid bills awaiting processing from the state; and
WHEREAS, the increase of uninsured and underinsured patients, sagging Medicare and Medicaid
reimbursements, as well as huge demands for capital needs at SSM’s other hospitals, have led to SSM’s
decision to close the doors of St. Francis Hospital in the next several months; and
WHEREAS, after exhausting efforts to find a buyer for the hospital, SSM has offered to give the hospital
away for free and has reached out to Chicago and national faith-based providers and other health
facilities.

5560

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Bureau of Health Services conduct a
feasibility analysis to explore the possibility of whether or not the acquisition of St. Francis Hospital at no
cost is a viable option for strengthening the Bureau’s ability to serve the uninsured and underinsured
population of Cook County and for increasing the Bureau’s revenue stream of Medicare and Medicaid
reimbursement.

RESOLUTION
08-R-107
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE PETER N. SILVESTRI, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY AND JOSEPH MARIO MORENO
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
RESOLUTION OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS IN SUPPORT OF
THE APPLICATION FOR PURCHASE OF THE ELGIN, JOLIET AND EASTERN RAILWAY
BY THE CANADIAN NATIONAL RAILWAY PENDING BEFORE THE UNITED STATES
DEPARTMENT OF TRANSPORTATION TO ENHANCE REGIONAL TRAIN SYSTEMS
WHEREAS, one third of the nation’s freight rail traffic moves to, from or through the Chicago area
every year making it the transportation hub of North America; and
WHEREAS, rail congestion has significantly slowed freight traffic through the Chicago region to the
point where it can now take a freight train 24 hours to travel the thirty miles through the City of Chicago,
slowing rail transportation nationwide; and
WHEREAS, opening up capacity on urban rail lines means that all rail traffic will move more efficiently
and smoothly through the city; and
WHEREAS, freight trains are three times more fuel-efficient and emit one-third less pollution than
trucks carrying comparable loads, thereby lessening the drain on the nation’s energy reserves; and
WHEREAS, a typical freight train carries the equivalent of 280 truck-trailer loads, thereby alleviating
highway congestion by keeping time-sensitive freight on the rails rather than diverting to highways; and
WHEREAS, rail transportation is crucial to the region economically touching five million jobs
nationwide; and

5562

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, if the problem of rail congestion in the region goes unchecked, it could cost the region $2
billion in production with impacts on 17,000 jobs over the next two decades; and
WHEREAS, the Chicago Region Environmental and Transportation Efficiency Program (CREATE) a
model public-private partnership, initiated more than five years ago, developed a comprehensive long
term plan that would revitalize the area’s transportation network by reconfiguring rail traffic through the
Chicago Metropolitan region; and
WHEREAS, the CREATE comprehensive plan still hasn’t received full government funding, even
though it has had wide support from every level of government, the private sector and a broad crosssection of non-governmental groups and organizations; and
WHEREAS, the Canadian National Railway Company, a founder and strong proponent of CREATE
since its inception, has proposed rerouting its traffic from the congested urban rail lines to the underutilized Elgin, Joliet and Eastern Railway at its own cost and expense, thereby opening up new capacity
on those urban lines; and
WHEREAS, by rerouting its traffic, the Canadian National Railway Company will relieve freight
congestion on many of Chicago’s regional rail lines, thereby reducing travel times, pollution from idling
trains and costs resulting from shipping delays.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Cook County Board of
Commissioners urges the Surface Transportation Board of the U.S. Department of Transportation to
approve the application of the Canadian National Railway Company to acquire the Elgin, Joliet and
Eastern Railway as a valuable enhancement of the region’s rail network; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be forwarded to the acting secretary of
the Surface Transportation Board, the members of the House of Representatives and Senators Richard
Durbin and Barack Obama from the great State of Illinois.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

5563

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
A RESOLUTION FOR ALL OUR KIDS CICERO EARLY CHILDHOOD NETWORK
WHEREAS, the All Our Kids (AOK) Cicero Early Childhood Network is a program operated through
the Cook County Department of Public Health and funded by the Illinois Department of Human Services;
and
WHEREAS, since 2000 the AOK Network has been serving the young children of Cicero to help them
get a healthy start in life, because early childhood development and learning is an integral foundation for
healthy adulthood; and
WHEREAS, the AOK Network is a community-based collaborative of over 60 agencies committed to
developing a high-quality, well-coordinated, easily accessible system of care promoting positive growth
and development for the 10,000 Cicero children under the age of five, as well as for their families; and
WHEREAS, the goal of the AOK Network is to ensure that: babies are born healthy, children remain
healthy and children enter school ready to learn and families are connected to the services that they need.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that I, Todd H. Stroger, along with the Cook County Board
of Commissioners, on behalf of the more than five million residents of Cook County, support the AOK
Cicero Early Childhood Network and commend their role in ensuring that the young children of Cicero
get the best start in life.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

08-R-109
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
A RESOLUTION HONORING EILEEN MULDOON
FOR HER WORK TREATING CHILDREN WITH CLEFT PALATES

5564

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, Eileen Muldoon recently returned from Santa Cruz, Bolivia, as a part of Operation Smile,
with a team of 46 volunteer doctors, nurses and non-medical personnel to treat children with cleft palates
and cleft lips; and
WHEREAS, Eileen Muldoon took care of children before and after their surgeries as a part of the
Operation Smile mission which performed approximately 150 surgeries during their 10 days in Bolivia;
and
WHEREAS, children born with cleft palates and cleft lips can have speech impediments and trouble
eating; and
WHEREAS, children with cleft palates and cleft lips can be shunned or made fun of to a point where
they no longer attend school and in some parts of the world, babies with cleft palates, that cannot eat, stop
getting fed; and
WHEREAS, Eileen Muldoon understands the rejection that children with cleft palates and cleft lips can
feel as she had a severe speech impediment, as a child, due to a cleft palate, which took three surgeries at
ages 2, 7 and 16 to successfully correct and also has a daughter that was born with a cleft palate, which
was repaired at 18 months old; and
WHEREAS, Eileen Muldoon, the daughter of Irish immigrants, was raised on the North Side of Chicago
and currently lives in Chicago’s Mt. Greenwood community with her husband, Ray, and her four
children; and
WHEREAS, Eileen Muldoon is a pediatric nurse at Mercy Hospital, in Chicago and is currently working
on her master’s degree in nursing at St. Xavier University.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, on
behalf of the more than 5 million residents of Cook County, gratefully acknowledge and thank Eileen
Muldoon for her dedicated service to the children of Cook County and the children of Santa Cruz,
Bolivia, and may a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered herewith.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

08-R-113
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ANTHONY J. PERAICA, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER, PRESIDENT, WILLIAM M. BEAVERS,
JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELIZABETH “LIZ” DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, MIKE QUIGLEY,
TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
ROBERT B. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
IN HONOR OF DEAN EMERITUS FRED F. HERZOG
WHEREAS, Almighty God in his infinite wisdom has called Fred Herzog from our midst on March 21,
2008 at the age of 100; and
WHEREAS, Fred Herzog was born into a loving family on September 21, 1907 in Prague; and
WHEREAS, three months later his family moved to Graz, Austria, where Herzog attended the local
grammar and secondary schools; and

5569

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, his intellectual prowess was nurtured by his father, the chief rabbi of Styria, Austria, and a
renowned university professor of antique oriental languages; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Herzog began his legal studies in Graz, Austria, and earned his law degree in 1931; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Herzog moved to Vienna where he served as a prosecutor and an assistant judge, before
he was appointed a judge for life in 1935; and
WHEREAS, the day after Hitler’s forces invaded Austria in 1938, Mr. Herzog was dismissed from his
post because he was a Jew; and
WHEREAS, this resulted in Mr. Herzog moving to Sweden in 1939 and coming to the United States in
1940; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Herzog arrived in New York in 1940, where he applied for and was turned down for a
dishwashing job that paid $12 per week because he had no prior dishwashing experience; and
WHEREAS, Mr. Herzog was able to obtain a fellowship from the University of Iowa College of Law,
where he graduated with high honors in 1942; and
WHEREAS, Fred Herzog moved to Chicago following his graduation and worked as an attorney in
private practice for several years before deciding he really wanted to teach; and
WHEREAS, Fred Herzog joined the faculty of Chicago-Kent, where he taught labor law, property,
legislation, trusts, and equity; and
WHEREAS, Illinois Governor Richard B. Ogilvie (Class of 1949), Illinois Supreme Court Justice
Thomas J. Moran (Class of 1950), and Homer J. Livingston, Jr., former president and CEO of the
Chicago Stock Exchange (Class of 1966) are among his former students; and
WHEREAS, Fred Herzog was named dean of the law school at Kent in 1970, shortly after the school
merged with the Illinois Institute of Technology and served in this capacity until 1973; and
WHEREAS, Fred Herzog accepted a position of first assistant attorney general of Illinois in 1973 and
remained with the office until 1976; and
WHEREAS, Fred Herzog served as dean of John Marshall Law School from 1976 to 1983, accepting the
title of Dean Emeritus upon his retirement; and
WHEREAS, Dean Herzog later returned to John Marshall as an interim dean, serving in this capacity
from 1990 to 1991; and
WHEREAS, Dean Herzog, a well respected lawyer, who earned numerous honors and awards throughout
his long career, considered teaching to be his favorite job, saying that “Teaching young people, that’s
what gave me the greatest satisfaction,” in an interview with the Chicago Sun-Times on the eve of his
100th birthday; and
WHEREAS, Dean Herzog leaves behind two loving sons, Steven and David, four loving grandchildren,
and thousands of people whose lives he has touched throughout his years as a professor of law, dean, and
mentor.

5570

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County do hereby offer their condolences to the family and friends of Dean Emeritus Fred Herzog who
will miss him deeply, and offers their most profound gratitude to Fred Herzog for the innumerable
contributions he has made to those students he has taught and inspired throughout his career.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

08-R-114
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
WHEREAS, Bo Diddley was born Ellas Otha Bates on December 30, 1928 in Macomb, Mississippi, he
migrated to Chicago with his adoptive family in the 1930’s legally embracing their McDaniel surname.
He studied the violin for twelve years before taking up the guitar in his early teens and it was at this time
he acquired the name Bo Diddley; and
WHEREAS, Bo Diddley began his legendary career in the mid 1940’s, known for popularizing one of
the foundational rhythms of rock and roll: the Bo Diddley beat, a distinctive African-based 5/4 rhythm
pattern imitated by other artists it has been an idiosyncratic and recurring element in rock and roll since its
beginning; and
WHEREAS, Bo Diddley’s illustrious career spanned more than five decades, a prolific songwriter and
guitarist, whose contributions forever changed the music industry. He was one of the first American
musicians to feature women in his band, and set up one of the first home studios. Long regarded as one
of the founding fathers of rock and roll he achieved crossover success with a laugh-filled exchange of jive
talk with his maraca player, a prelude to today’s rap genre; and
WHEREAS, Bo Diddley has received numerous honors throughout his life, most recently in 1987 he was
inducted into the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame; in 1996, he received a Lifetime Achievement Award from
the Rhythm and Blues Foundation, and in 1998 a Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award. At the dawn of
the millennium he was inducted into the Mississippi Musicians Hall of Fame, in 2002 he received a
Pioneer in Entertainment Award from the National Association of Black Broadcasters and in 2007 Bo
Diddley received the Governors Award of Excellence in the Arts for Lifetime Achievement from his
home state of Mississippi; and
WHEREAS, On April 14, 2008 KoKo Taylor and her Foundation will honor Bo Diddley as a vocal
advocate for early rock and rollers on the subject of deceptive practices, underpayment, and bad contracts
as well as acknowledging his quintessential talents forever endearing him to the music loving community.

5571

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby commend Bo Diddley for his accomplishments and contributions to contemporary music; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to Mr. Ellas McDaniel,
“Bo Diddley”.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

AND TODD H. STROGER, PRESIDENT

PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, ROBERT B. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called Stanley S. Wiczus from our midst; and
WHEREAS, Stanley S. Wiczus was known with great affection as "Big Sta" to his many friends; and
WHEREAS, Stanley S. Wiczus was the beloved husband of Mary (nee Farcau) Wiczus; and
WHEREAS, Stanley S. Wiczus was the loving father of Juliann (Timothy) Newton, and Michael J.
(C.F.D.) Wiczus; and
WHEREAS, Stanley S. Wiczus was the fond grandfather of Kelly, and Lindsay Newton, and dear
brother of the late Helen Ludwig, and Tony Talmont; and
WHEREAS, Stanley S. Wiczus served and protected the citizens of Chicago as a Lieutenant with Engine
Company 29 of the Chicago Fire Department; and
WHEREAS, Stanley S. Wiczus bravely answered the call of his country during the Second World War
and defended the cause of freedom in the United States Air Force, where he served with uncommon valor;
and
WHEREAS, Stanley S. Wiczus was a proud member in good standing of the Hamburg Club; and
WHEREAS, all who knew him will attest that Stanley S. Wiczus was a kind and compassionate man,
virtuous of character and gentle in spirit, admired and respected by his many friends and neighbors, and
dearly loved by his family.

5577

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008

Board does hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and many
friends of Stanley S. Wiczus, and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body, and a suitable copy of same be tendered to the family of Stanley S. Wiczus, that his memory may
be so honored and ever cherished.

AND ROBERT B. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS

5579

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
IN MEMORY OF VINCENT L. GILLON
WHEREAS, Vincent Gillon passed away on March 17, 2008; and
WHEREAS, Vincent Gillon was as a tireless organizer and advocate for those struggling to maintain
drug and alcohol free lives and he helped families in Evanston, Rogers Park and the neighborhoods of
Cook County; and
WHEREAS, Vincent Gillon grew up in the Gresham neighborhood of Chicago and after graduating from
Calumet High School, served a six-year tour in the United States Army that included service in Vietnam;
and
WHEREAS, upon return to civilian life, Vincent Gillon faced and triumphed over the evils of addiction,
racism and post war trauma; and
WHEREAS, after besting his addiction, Vincent Gillon enrolled at National-Louis University and
worked in the outpatient substance-abuse programs at Chicago Lakeshore Hospital, and the REST shelter
in Uptown; and
WHEREAS, working in tandem with Ray Lee, Vincent Gillon developed a model outreach program for
Better Existence with HIV (BEHIV) in Evanston, Rogers Park and Edgewater; and
WHEREAS, Vincent Gillon earned a bachelor’s degree in applied behavioral sciences and a master’s
degree in human services counseling from National Louis; and
WHEREAS, in 1998, Vincent Gillon founded CAREPOINT Adult, Child and Family Association in
Evanston to improve the lives of families, children and adults through a comprehensive range of social,
welfare and health-related services; and
WHEREAS, CAREPOINT’s vision of a society in which all families, children and adults are able to
achieve quality of life through equal access and advocacy for services offered with dignity and respect
was institutionalized by Vince Gillon and his staff; and
WHEREAS, Vincent Gillon was honored for his work with CAREPOINT Adult, Child and Family
Association by the National Association for the Advancement of Colored People - NAACP, the Chicago
Defender, the Illinois Department of Public Health, and was recently featured by Harry Porterfield on
ABC News as “Someone You Should Know”; and
WHEREAS, all those who knew Vincent Gillon recognized his intense dedication to helping others face
their personal demons and placing them on the road to recovery; and
WHEREAS, Vincent Gillon is survived by his wife, Charisee; his mother, Louise Gillon; his son, Parris
Blake; his daughters, Simone, Victoria and Aliya; his stepdaughters, Ashley and Tierra; his brother, Kurt;
and his sister, Regina; and
WHEREAS, Vincent Gillon will be deeply missed and forever treasured by all who knew him and the
people of Cook County owe a debt of gratitude to Vincent Gillon for his outstanding civic involvement
and extensive contributions to the community.

5580

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and friends of Vincent
Gillon and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of
Vincent Gillon so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

MIKE QUIGLEY, TIMOTHY O. SCHNEIDER, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
ROBERT B. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
HONORING NORTHBROOK PARK DISTRICT
EXECUTIVE DIRECTOR ED HARVEY ON HIS RETIREMENT
WHEREAS, Ed Harvey will be retiring as Executive Director of the Northbrook Park District on May
16, 2008; and
WHEREAS, Ed Harvey has served as Executive Director of the Northbrook Park District for 20 years
since 1988, prior to coming to Northbrook Ed Harvey served as Director of Operations for the Champaign
Park District for 10 years, and as Supervisor of Operations for the Urbana Park District from 1971 to
1978; and
WHEREAS, under the leadership of Ed Harvey, the Northbrook Park District has grown into a stellar
example of the valuable services and programs park district’s can provide their residents; and

5581

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, as Executive Director Ed Harvey had the vision to recognize the opportunity that restoring
the Anetsberger property would have for the Village of Northbrook and its residents; and
WHEREAS, Ed Harvey supervised the creation of the Techny Prairie Park and fields from the
Anetsberger property, providing open space and much needed playing fields for the community, and was
involved in all aspects of the project including his work on the referendum by informing the public of the
value of the property to the Village of Northbrook and its residents; and
WHEREAS, Ed Harvey also served on numerous village boards including the Comprehensive Plan
Committee, the Bike Trail Task Force, and helped develop public lands dedication standards and was
responsible for successfully securing millions in restoration/development grants; and
WHEREAS, Ed Harvey is a dedicated lifetime supporter of the North Shore Special Recreation
Association (NSSRA), serving children with developmental disabilities and their families; and
WHEREAS, Ed Harvey has been active in the community as a member and President of the Northbrook
Rotary Club, member of the Northbrook Civic Foundation and the Northbrook Chamber of Commerce.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners honors Ed
Harvey on the occasion of his retirement and for his dedication and leadership as he guided the
Northbrook Park District to the betterment of its residents and staff; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Ed Harvey to
commemorate this auspicious occasion.
Approved and adopted this 9th day of April 2008.
TODD H. STROGER, President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Construction of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice
on Tuesday, April 8, 2008 at the hour of 1:15 P.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building, 118
North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.

5641

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
Your Committee has considered the following items and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
292320

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Bruce Washington, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated January 25, 2008.
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids for the Bureau of Health Services, Bid Package #2. The
project includes the build-out of pharmacies at Fantus Clinic, Oak Forest Hospital of
Cook County and Stroger Hospital of Cook County. It is respectfully requested that this
Honorable Body approve this request.
Reason:

This project will require a contractor to obtain all regulatory and construction
permits, and provide all labor, equipment and materials necessary to properly
renovate and build out the pharmacies at three locations. The scope of this
project will require general construction, plumbing and electrical work.

Bond Issue (33000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
*Referred to the Committee on Construction on 02/20/08.
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Sims, moved approval of Communication No.
292320. The motion carried unanimously.
292321

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Bruce Washington, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated January 25, 2008.
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids for the Countywide Telecommunication Wiring Installation
Phase 2A Bid Package #2 for Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County (OFHCC). It is
respectfully requested that this Honorable Body approve this request.
Reason:

The project will include upgrading the voice and data infrastructure wiring for
fiber optic and copper backbone with category 5e wire on the Oak Forest
Hospital of Cook County campus. The campus telecom data center, located in
Building ‘A’, will be upgraded according to the specifications outlined by the
Bureau of Information Technology & Automation (BITA). All major
buildings (approximately 50) on the OFHCC campus will be connected to the
telecom data center. All workstation drops will be upgraded. Twelve new
telecommunication closets will be built within various buildings on the
OFHCC campus. The remaining 50 closets will be upgraded, as required,
based on the BITA specifications. A wireless local area network (LAN) will
be installed with access points throughout the campus. All patient rooms will
be wired with voice/data drops.

Bond Issue (20000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
*Referred to the Committee on Construction on 02/20/08.

5642

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Sims, moved approval of Communication No.
292321. The motion carried unanimously.
292322

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Bruce Washington, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated January 25, 2008.
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization to enter into a

292323

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Bruce Washington, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated January 25, 2008.
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization to enter into a
professional services contract with PARKING GARAGE PARTNERS, Chicago,
Illinois, selected from the Request for Qualifications/Proposals process. The services
required are for the Stroger Hospital of Cook County Campus-Parking Structure
Expansion, Phase IIB. It is respectfully requested that this Honorable Body approve this
request.
Reason:

The services provide for architectural and engineering services as well as
related services for the new construction of the Stroger Hospital of Cook
County Campus Parking Structure Expansion, Phase IIB, at 1800 West Polk
Street, Chicago, Illinois. The existing parking structure was completed and
opened in the year 1999 and is approximately 545,000 total square feet. It has
2-levels below grade and 5-levels at grade and above. The Project consists of
expanding the current 1,340 space parking facility by adding 1,760 more
parking spaces; to bring the total to 3,100 spaces. This includes the design of
an above ground walkway (sky bridge) connecting the garage with the new
hospital, the Hektoen Institute Building and other campus buildings;
recommendation and design of snow removal system for the entire garage;
automatic landscaping watering system and recommend, design and detail of
restoration of all damaged surfaces of the existing parking structure.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $3,450.000.00. Bond Issue (28000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
*Referred to the Committee on Construction on 02/20/08.

5643

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Sims, moved approval of Communication No.
292323.
Commissioner Schneider stated that eight (8) firms were listed on the RFP; of the eight (8) the responding
party to whom the consulting contract was given is not one of the firms listed on the RFP.
Mr. Washington explained that two (2) of the firms joined and they joined in the joint venture.
Commissioner Schneider stated that he never received the individual contracts from the original RFP; he
doesn’t have the contract of the coalition of the two contracts.
Chairman Murphy stated to Commissioner Schneider that he is entitled to receive any information that he
requests; but normally the Commissioners do not review all of the contracts. Rather, the Commissioners
depend on the individuals who are running the departments to know what is best for the County.
Commissioner Schneider, seconded by Commissioner Gorman, moved to defer Communication No.
292323. The motion carried unanimously.

292966

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Bruce Washington, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated February 21, 2008.
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization to enter into a
professional services contract with WMA Consulting Engineers, Chicago, Illinois,
selected from the Request for Qualifications/Proposals process. The services required are
design and construction administration for the repair and replacement of clean steam
piping at Stroger Hospital of Cook County. It is respectfully requested that this
Honorable Body approve this request.
Reason:

This project is required due to extensive corrosion to the existing clean steam
system. This project will include the evaluation of the existing system for the
design for repair and replacement and/or for the use of an alternate method. The
actual remediation of the project will be performed in two phases.
Phase One Contract Documents will include preliminary remediation of the
system including water treatment and steam filters. Phase Two Contract
Documents will include replacement of piping and fittings and other system
components and add components as necessary.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $2,150,000.00. Bond Issue (28000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
Vendor has met the Minority and Women Business Enterprise Ordinance.
*Referred to the Committee on Construction, as Amended on 02/20/08.
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Sims, moved approval of Communication No.
292966.

5645

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
Chairman Murphy asked if the item was time sensitive.
Bruce Washington, Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy, stated that the Office of Capital
Planning and Policy would like for the Committee to move forward due to the life safety issues that exist
at the hospital.
Mr. Washington further stated that in January the Office of Capital Planning and Policy received a letter
from the hospital speaking to the deteriorating piping, the corrosion that exists throughout the facility and
the potential for leaking steam to harm both patients and employees.
In conclusion Mr. Washington distributed photographs illustrating the conditions that exist.
Commissioner Silvestri asked why it took three months if it was an emergency.
Mr. Washington stated that back in January the Office of Capital Planning and Policy started the review
of the RFP.
Commissioner Silvestri inquired as to how many firms responded to the RFP.
