REPORT OF THE NOMINATING COMMITTEE OF THE INTERIM BOARD OF DIRECTORS
OF THE COOK COUNTY BUREAU OF HEALTH
March 20, 2008
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County
ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Richard Sewell - Illinois Public Health Association; Vice Chairman Larry
Goodman, MD - Civic Committee of the Commercial Club of Chicago; Secretary Aida L.
Giachello, Ph.D. - Midwest Latino Health Research Center; Terry Mason, MD - Chicago
Department of Public Health; Thomas Balanoff - Chicago Federation of Labor; William
Werner, MD - Chicago Medical Society; Sharon Jones - Chicago Urban League;
Laurence Msall - Civic Federation of Chicago; Niva Lubin-Johnson, MD - Cook County
Physicians Association; Margie Schaps - Health and Medicine Policy Research Group;
Kevin Scanlan - Metropolitan Chicago Healthcare Council; and Victoria Bigelow Suburban Primary Health Care Council (12)

Absent:

Mark Newton - Association of Community Safety Net Hospitals; and Richard Clarke Healthcare Financial Management Association (2)

Also Present:

The Honorable Todd H. Stroger, President of the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County and Cook County Commissioners Jerry Butler, John P. Daley, Anthony J.
Peraica, Mike Quigley, Robert B. Steele and Larry Suffredin (6); Patrick T. Driscoll, Jr. Deputy State’s Attorney, Chief, Civil Actions Bureau; Richard Velázquez - Special
Counsel to President Todd H. Stroger; and Matthew B. DeLeon - Secretary to the Board
of Commissioners of Cook County

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Nominating Committee of the Interim Board of Directors of the Cook County Bureau of Health met
pursuant to notice on Thursday, March 20, 2008 at the hour of 11:00 A.M. in the Board Room, Room
569, County Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
The purpose of the meeting was to select a chair of the Nominating Committee and to conduct discussion
concerning the nomination and recommendation of candidates for the office of Director of the Interim
Board of Directors.
This convening of the designated representatives of each of the organizations which comprise the
Nominating Committee was pursuant to Cook County Ordinance 08-O-22, approved and adopted on
February 29, 2008, which states:

5649

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
Sec. 38.2.a. Members of the IBOD shall be selected by the following process.
Sec 38-2.a(i). A Nominating Committee shall be convened no later than 14 days
after enactment of this ordinance. This Nominating Committee shall include one
person designated by each of the following organizations which so agree to
participate as its representative: the Civic Federation of Chicago, the Civic
Committee of the Commercial Club of Chicago, the Chicago Urban League, the
Healthcare Financial Management Association, the Suburban Primary Health Care
Council, the Illinois Public Health Association, the Metropolitan Chicago
Healthcare Council, the Health and Medicine Policy Research Group, the Chicago
Department of Public Health, the Cook County Physicians Association, the Chicago
Federation of Labor, the Chicago Medical Society, and the Association of
Community Safety Net Hospitals, and the Midwest Latino Health Research Center.
The Nominating Committee shall elect its chair from its own ranks. All decisions
shall be by majority vote. The Nominating Committee shall recommend twenty (20)
candidates for nomination and shall transmit their names and qualifications to the
President of the Cook County Board within 30 days of the Nominating Committee’s
convening.
President Todd H. Stroger presided over the opening of the meeting and requested that a roll call of the
members of the Nominating Committee be taken by Matthew B. DeLeon, Secretary to the Board of
Commissioners of Cook County.
A quorum was established. President Stroger welcomed the representatives and gave a brief statement on
recent achievements and future hopes for the Bureau of Health Services.
Richard Velázquez, Special Counsel to President Todd H. Stroger, provided the Nominating Committee
members with an overview of Cook County Ordinance 08-O-22.
President Stroger opened the floor for nominations for Chairman of the Nominating Committee.
A motion was made by Dr. Lubin-Johnson, seconded by Dr. Giachello, to nominate Mr. Richard
Sewell as Chairman of the Nominating Committee.
A motion was made by Mr. Werner, seconded by Mr. Msall, to nominate Dr. Larry Goodman as
Chairman of the Nominating Committee.
Following discussion, both nominating motions were withdrawn by their respective sponsors.
A motion was made by Dr. Mason, seconded by Mr. Balanoff, to nominate Mr. Richard Sewell as
Chairman and Dr. Larry Goodman as Vice Chairman of the Nominating Committee. The motion
carried unanimously.
Chairman Sewell in the Chair.
A motion was made by Dr. Mason, seconded by Ms. Schaps, to nominate Dr. Aida Giachello as
Secretary of the Nominating Committee. The motion carried unanimously.
Discussion followed on how best to proceed in order to accomplish the directives stated in the Ordinance.

5650

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
A motion was made by Dr. Mason, seconded by Secretary Giachello, that among the twenty names
submitted to the President, at least one person should be nominated for the Governing Board per
area of qualification categories listed in Section 38.2.b. of the Ordinance, and a recommendation
should be made to the President that his selection be representative of persons for each of these
areas.
Dr. Lubin-Johnson moved to amend the motion, to combine the areas of qualification categories
“Health Care Management” and “Clinical Medicine” referenced in Section 38.2.b. of the Ordinance
into one area of qualification category. The motion to amend died due to lack of a second.
Mr. Msall moved to amend the motion, to recognize the primary area of expertise as experience in
the governance of a large and complex health care system. The motion to amend died due to lack of
a second.
Ms. Jones, seconded by Mr. Balanoff, moved to table the motion. The motion carried. Dr. Mason
voted no.
A discussion began regarding potential conflict of interest matters. Ms. Schaps inquired whether
employees of Cook County or those serving on the Nominating Committee could be nominated to the
Interim Board of Directors.
Mr. Velázquez replied that he believed that those serving on the Nominating Committee could be
nominated, but employees of Cook County could not be nominated.
Mr. Msall inquired whether the nominations would be subject to any restrictions beyond conflict of
interest issues.
Mr. Velázquez replied that Cook County has a residency requirement for their employees, however this
ordinance is silent with regard to a residency requirement.
Dr. Mason noted that communications between Nominating Committee members may be subject to the
Open Meetings Act. He asked for further clarification on the matter.
Mr. Velázquez advised the members that their deliberations were subject to the Open Meetings Act,
which ensures that public business is discussed in a public forum. Communications between more than
four members of the Committee without prior notice to the public in the form of a meeting notice would
be prohibited under the Act.
Mr. Balanoff inquired whether members could submit proposed candidates for nomination to the
Chairman electronically without being subject to the Open Meetings Act.
Mr. Velázquez replied affirmatively. He stated that the submissions could be made to the Chairman
electronically; however an electronic communication that invites discussion and deliberation would be
subject to the Act and should be transmitted to no more than four members.
Secretary Giachello indicated that it would be optimal to receive the biographies and resumes of the
proposed candidates prior to deliberations.
Chairman Sewell suggested that members send proposed nominees and background information to him;
when a meeting notice is sent, the members will receive the background information on the proposed
candidates as backup information.

5651

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
Dr. Lubin-Johnson, seconded by Ms. Bigelow, moved that committee members be limited to six
proposed candidates for the first round of deliberations. The motion carried unanimously.
Dr. Mason clarified the procedures agreed upon by the committee members for deliberations. The
committee members would submit proposed candidates to the Chairman. A matrix would be developed
for members for the next meeting, which would identify the area of qualifications the proposed candidate
falls within. However, members are not precluded from proposing candidates who do not fall within the
areas of qualifications as listed in Section 38.2.b. of the Ordinance.
Mr. Msall inquired whether the committee could consider the proposed candidates in executive session.
Mr. Velázquez relied in the affirmative. He cited the specific exception allowed under the Open Meetings
Act that allows deliberation of these matters in closed session.
Mr. Msall, seconded by Dr. Lubin-Johnson, moved that the committee meet in executive session to
present and discuss the proposed candidates at their next meeting. The motion carried
unanimously.
Dr. Lubin-Johnson, seconded by Ms. Jones, moved to set the submission deadline for the first
round of proposed candidates to be sent to the Chairman for Monday, March 31, 2008 at 5:00 p.m.
The motion carried. Ms. Schaps voted no.
Mr. Balanoff, seconded by Mr. Msall, moved to adopt Robert’s Rules of Order, latest edition. The
motion carried unanimously.
Mr. Balanoff, seconded by Dr. Lubin-Johnson, moved to suspend the portion of Robert’s Rules to
allow use of substitute individuals to represent organizations. The motion carried unanimously.
Dr. Lubin-Johnson, seconded by Ms. Jones, moved to set the submission deadline for the first
round of proposed candidates to be sent to the Chairman for Friday, March 28, 2008.
Mr. Balanoff, seconded by Mr. Msall, moved to amend the motion to change the submission
deadline for the first round of proposed candidates to be sent to the Chairman for Monday, March
31, 2008 in order that they be presented to the committee for a meeting to be held on Friday, April
4, 2008 at 1:00 p.m. The motion carried unanimously.
On the main motion, as amended, a voice vote was taken. The motion carried unanimously.
Dr. Mason reiterated his interest in addressing the issue of areas of qualification categories not included in
Section 38.2.b. of the Ordinance.
Chairman Sewell stated that two such categories not mentioned in the Ordinance were “Research” and
“Public Health”.
A consensus was reached among committee members on subsequent meeting dates. A meeting date of
Monday, April 7, 2008 at 9:00 a.m. was agreed upon for a possible reconvening date if the Friday, April
4, 2008 meeting is recessed. Additionally, the committee agreed on a meeting date of Monday, April 14,
2008 at 1:00 p.m.

5652

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
Meeting Dates:

Monday, April 7, 2008 at 9:00 a.m.*

* If necessary – this date set as possible reconvening date if the April 4, 2008 meeting is recessed.
Ms. Jones, seconded by Secretary Giachello, moved to adjourn the meeting. The motion carried
and the meeting was adjourned.

of Cook County met pursuant to notice on Wednesday, April 9, 2008 at the hour of 9:30 A.M. in the
Board Room, Room 569, County Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following items and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
291513

SUPPORTING AND ENDORSING THE MISSION, OBJECTIVES AND FUTURE OF
THE COOK COUNTY SUBURBAN ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT COMMISSION
(CCSEDC) (PROPOSED RESOLUTION). Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored
by Deborah Sims, County Commissioner, Co-Sponsored by Joan Patricia Murphy,
County Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Administration and County Board of Cook County are dedicated to
establishing a stable and progressive financial future for the County; and
WHEREAS, the Administration and County Board of Cook County believe that
responsible economic development is at the heart of future financial stability and growth
of the County; and
WHEREAS, the Administration and County Board of Cook County understand that
responsible economic development will take advantage of federal resources that support
and encourage new and emerging sustainable, environmentally-sound guidelines,
designs, technologies and practices which meet U.S. Green Building Council and
Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design (LEED) standards; and
WHEREAS, the Administration and County Board of Cook County understand that
sustainable and responsible economic development will create a critical and necessary
revenue generation mechanism; and
WHEREAS, the Administration and County Board of Cook County are committed to
effective revenue generation as a central means by which to address the financial
challenges of the County; and
WHEREAS, the Administration and County Board of Cook County believe that South
Cook County represents a viable and valuable region in which to establish the initial
long-term economic development and revenue generation initiative; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Suburban Economic Development Commission
(CCSEDC) was incorporated as of November 1, 2007 as a not-for-profit, public-private,
multi-jurisdictional economic development vehicle comprised of four suburban councils
of municipal government and a Chairperson from suburban Cook County; and

5654

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, the Cook County Suburban Economic Development Commission supplants
Enterpriz Cook County which was voluntarily dissolved on October 31, 2007; and
WHEREAS, the mission of the Cook County Suburban Economic Development
Commission is to identify, organize and mobilize public and private mechanisms and
resources that will create and expand business and business development, thereby
producing economic growth, new business enterprises, living-wage jobs and new
revenues throughout suburban Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Suburban Economic Development Commission is funded
by non-governmental corporate donations, contracts and contributions.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of
Commissioners supports and endorses the mission, objectives and future of the Cook
County Suburban Economic Development Commission (CCSEDC); furthermore the
Board encourages the active participation of Cook County government in a unified
approach to increased economic development in Cook County.
* Deferred at the meeting of the Real Estate & Business & Economic Development
Subcommittee on 04/09/08.
Commissioner Schneider, seconded by Commissioner Gorman, moved to defer Communication No.
291513. The motion carried unanimously.
291514

AN ORDINANCE REGARDING THE COOK COUNTY SUBURBAN ECONOMIC
DEVELOPMENT COMMISSION (CCSEDC) (PROPOSED ORDINANCE).
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Deborah Sims, County Commissioner.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
BE IT ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners, that:
WHEREAS, effective, unified and forward-looking economic development stands as a
vitally important vehicle for financial stability and revenue generation; and
WHEREAS, economic vitality, financial stability and new revenue generation are
determined to be important to the future of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Suburban Economic Development Commission was
established to accelerate, coordinate and expedite economic development in suburban
Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the success of the Cook County Suburban Economic Development
Commission will result in economic vitality, financial stability and new revenue
generation in Cook County; and

5655

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
WHEREAS, the Cook County Suburban Economic Development Commission will take
advantage of federal resources that support and encourage new and emerging sustainable,
environmentally-sound guidelines, designs, technologies and practices which meet U.S.
Green Building Council and Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design (LEED)
standards; and
WHEREAS, a revised system of classifying real estate for the purposes of development
and assessment is important to the long-term success of the Cook County Suburban
Economic Development Commission; and
WHEREAS, the long-term success of the Cook County Suburban Economic
Development Commission is important to the long-term financial growth and stability of
Cook County.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED, by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners that:

5658

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
BUREAU OF ADMINISTRATION
AUTHORIZATION TO RESCIND A PREVIOUSLY APPROVED CONTRACT
AND AUTHORIZATION TO ENTER INTO A NEW CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 26, 2008 from
MARK KILGALLON, Chief Administrative Officer, Bureau of Administration
requesting authorization to enter into a professional services contract with Integrys Energy Services,
Chicago, Illinois, for the purchase and delivery of natural gas for the County’s heating and cooling needs.
On February 6, 2008, the Board approved entering into a contract with Enbridge Gas Services (U.S.) Inc.,
however, negotiations conducted by the State’s Attorney’s Office with Enbridge were unsuccessful and
did not result in an agreement on contract terms.
Further requesting that Item #54 from the February 6, 2008 Board Agenda authorizing the Purchasing
Agent to enter into an agreement with Enbridge Gas Services (U.S.), Inc., Appleton, Wisconsin, be
rescinded.
To participate in the deregulated natural gas market, Integrys Energy Services will act as the exclusive
agent for all matters related to the procurement and delivery of natural gas and execute all documents as
may be necessary to carry out and comply with the provisions of the Illinois Commerce Commission’s
conditions of service for public utilities serving Cook County for customer owned gas.
On July 31, 2007, the Board of Commissioners authorized the Bureau of Administration to solicit
proposals through a Request for Proposals (RFP) process for the procurement and delivery of natural gas.
Request for Proposals were issued resulting in the submission of six responses. Evaluation of the
proposals was based upon the (1) margin cost per therm above the index cost of natural gas, (2) firm’s
experience, (3) firm’s financial stability and credit rating, and (4) firm’s ability to meet the MBE/WBE
requirements of the County.
Integrys Energy Services is the County’s current natural gas supplier with a proven track record and was
the second lowest cost proposal. Integrys proposes a margin cost of $0.0020 per therm of natural gas
above the index cost. Margin cost accounts for less than 0.3% of the County’s total gas costs. The
County currently uses an average of 13.7 million therms per year resulting in an estimated annual cost of
$27,484.00 for Integrys’ professional administrative services. The County’s estimated FY 2008 natural
gas costs are $15.9 million.
With approval of the service agreement herein, respectfully request that the Chief Administrative Officer,
or his designee, be authorized to execute, on behalf of the County of Cook, all documents necessary to
implement and administer the service agreement.
All natural gas costs will be charged against the annual appropriation for the utility gas funds for each
using department. (499-422, 500-422, 564-422, 891-422, 894-422, 897-422 and 898-422 Accounts).
Contract Period: May 1, 2008 through April 30, 2012. Requisition No. 84900010.
Approval of this item would commit Fiscal Year 2008 and future year funds.

DEPARTMENT OF BUDGET AND MANAGEMENT SERVICES
REPORT
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 27, 2008 from
JARESE A. WILSON, Director, Department of Budget and Management Services
Subject: 1st Quarter Performance Report
submitting herewith a copy of the 1st Quarter Performance Reporting that highlights performance data
associated with Cook County Departments Services, Activities and Programs. This report is a starting
point when used in budgeting, long-term planning and goal setting, meaningful performance measures
will assist County Officials and Citizens in identifying future decisions regarding resources allocation and
service delivery. The 1st Quarter report will continue to be developed for subsequent quarters of FY 2008
to provide the means to share data on a range of programs, benchmark the County’s performance to
comparable jurisdictions, and improve service delivery through the application of best management
practices and efficient use of resources.
In the 1st Quarter Performance Report, we would like to highlight a Cook County Department that has
shown an especially useful performance measure and recognize their efforts. The Adult Probation
Department performance measure of “percentage of active standard probation cases being supervised
under Evidence Based Practices (EBP) - related procedures” should be acknowledged. The Adult
Probation Department is well above their target that indicates that community corrections programs that
are implemented have a direct impact and may lower offender risk and reduces recidivism.

DEPARTMENT OF ENVIRONMENTAL CONTROL
GRANT AWARD
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 6, 2008 from
KEVIN GIVENS, Director, Department of Environmental Control
requesting authorization to accept a grant award in the amount of $103,297.00 from the United States
Environmental Protection Agency (USEPA) Region V – CFDA 66.034 for the Cook County Midwest
Clean Diesel Initiative Project. The objectives of the Cook County Midwest Clean Diesel Initiative
Project are to reduce the emissions of carbon monoxide and fine particulate matter from 30 diesel trucks
operated by the Cook County Highway Department by installing U.S. Environmental Protection Agency
verified diesel retrofit technology in addition to initiating an aggressive awareness campaign targeting
Cook County employees and the general public.
This grant does not require a cash match.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $103,297.00. Funding period: January 1, 2008 through
December 31, 2009.
The Budget Department has received all requisite documents, and determined the fiscal impact on Cook
County, if any.

the Department of Environmental Control be approved and that the Proper Officials be authorized to sign
on behalf of Cook County. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 10, 2008 from
RUPERT F. GRAHAM, JR., P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Motor Fuel Tax Project
Appropriating Resolution
Oakton Street,
Skokie Boulevard to McCormick Boulevard
in the Village of Skokie in County Board District #13
Section: 03-A6728-02-EG
Centerline Mileage: 1.84 miles
Fiscal Impact: $90,000.00 from the Motor Fuel Tax Fund (600-600 Account)
08-R-123
RESOLUTION
APPROPRIATING RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE TODD H. STROGER
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, by the County Board of Commissioner of Cook County, Illinois, that
the following described County highway be improved under the Illinois Highway Code:
County Highway A67, Oakton Street, beginning at a point near Skokie Boulevard and extending along
said route in an easterly direction to a point near McCormick Boulevard, a distance of approximately 1.84
miles; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the appropriation shall be for paying the County’s share (50%) of
design engineering and plan preparation costs, including final construction plans, estimates and
specifications, contract documents and County reviews in accordance with a formal agreement with the
Village of Skokie and shall be designated as Section: 03-A6728-02-EG; and

5680

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the improvement shall be designed by an outside engineering
consultant contracted by the Village of Skokie; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that there is hereby appropriated the sum of Ninety Thousand and
No/100 Dollars, ($90,000.00) from the County’s allotment of Motor Fuel Tax Funds for the design of this
improvement; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Clerk is hereby directed to transmit two (2) certified copies of
this Resolution to the District Office of the Illinois Department of Transportation.
April 9, 2008
_________________________
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the Appropriating Resolution be
approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

5682

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
JUDICIARY
CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with the Chicago Bar
Foundation (CBF), Chicago, Illinois, to provide legal advice to pro-se litigants in the Forcible Entry and
Detainer Section of the First Municipal District. CBF is recommended as a result of a Request for
Proposal (RFP) process as a qualified provider with the lowest proposed cost.
Reason:

This contract proposal requires CBF to staff and supervise the advice desk on the sixth floor
of the Richard J. Daley Center. Approximately 4,000 and 4,200 pro se, working poor litigants
are expected to receive free legal advice desk services each year during the proposed contract
period. Historically, the majority assisted have been female African Americans with children.
About 18 percent have been persons with disabilities. Also, the advice desk staff provides
full representation through motion practice, discovery, and trial for more than 100 qualified
tenants in some eviction cases each year.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $395,983.00 (Year 2008 - $83,750.00; Year 2009 - $129,928.00; Year 2010 $137,453.00; and Year 2011 - $34,852.00). Contract period: March 1, 2008 through February 28, 2011.
(300-260 Account). Requisition No. 80300003.
Approval of this item commits Fiscal Year 2008 and future year funds.
_________________________
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

LEASE AGREEMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 17, 2008 from
RAYMOND MULDOON, Director, Real Estate Management Division
respectfully requesting authorization to enter into a lease agreement with Plaza Azteca, Inc. for a site at
26th and Washtenaw, to be used for the operation of special events including outdoor “Charreadas”,
Mexican style rodeos, concerts, dances, markets, carnivals and community festivals.
A Request for Proposals (RFP) for special events was issued by the Purchasing Agent on February 14,
2008. One proposal was received. A lease has been proposed rather than a license, in order to allow for
the staging of additional events, and to allow for the upgrading of improvements and construction of
semi-permanent facilities to better serve the public attending the events. Such an agreement is anticipated
to increase the revenues to the County.
Authorization is hereby requested to execute a ground lease with Plaza Azteca, Inc. on the terms set forth
below. This lease will allow Plaza Azteca, Inc. to stage events during the 2008 summer season, while
working with the Office of the President, the Bureau of Capital, Planning and Facilities Management to
obtain approval for improvements to the site. If approved by the Administration, it is anticipated that
improvements would be constructed by the Tenant prior to the 2009 summer season. Details are:
Tenant:

Plaza Azteca, Inc.

Term:

April 1, 2008 through March 31, 2012

Option Term:

Tenant shall have an option to renew the lease for an additional four (4) years,
subject to cancellation if the County decides to use the site for government
purposes. The parties may mutually agree to an additional four (4) year renewal,
subject to approval by the County Board.

5694

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
Right to Terminate:

The County has a right to terminate if the site is needed for a government
purpose. If improvements have been approved and constructed by the Tenant,
then such termination shall be subject to reimbursement by the County of the
unamortized cost of the Tenant’s approved improvements, not to exceed
$750,000.00. The Tenant may terminate if the company cannot obtain permits for
its events or improvements.

Base Rent:

$85,000.00 per year for the use of the site, plus $1,500.00 per day for use of the
parking structure, adjusted annually based on the Consumer Price Index.

Percentage Rent:

3% of total gross revenues, in excess of $500,000.00; 5% of gross revenues in
excess of $2,000,000.00.

Taxes:

Licensee will pay all applicable taxes, including leasehold taxes, sales taxes and
amusement taxes.
_________________________

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the lease agreement be approved
and that the Proper Officials be authorized to sign on behalf of the County. The motion carried.
Commissioners Peraica, Quigley and Suffredin voted “no.

DECLARATION OF EXCESS LAND
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 4, 2008
RAYMOND MULDOON, Director, Real Estate Management Division
requesting authorization to have certain property declared as “excess” by the Board of Commissioners of
Cook County, to conduct an appraisal of the property and to negotiate with the Town of Cicero (“Cicero”)
for the sale of the property by Quit Claim Deed. The interest of the Town of Cicero in this land is to
facilitate future redevelopment of the Cicero Avenue corridor at 31st Street. Upon completion of
appraisals and negotiation of terms of sale, this transaction will be presented to this Board for approval in
accordance with the Local Government Property Transfer Act (50 ILCS 605/1 et seq).

5699

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
The subject property encompasses a portion of the southwest and northwest frontage roads located south
of 31st Street just east of Cicero Avenue in Cook County District #7. The land being an area of
approximately 98,280 Square Feet (2.256 acres), in the West 1/2 of the N.W. 1/4 of Section 34, Township
39 North, Range 13, in the Town of Cicero, Cook County, Illinois.
It has been determined by all agencies involved that the subject property is no longer needed for County
purposes and can be released for sale.
Approval recommended.
_________________________
In accordance with Cook County Code Section 2-108(z)(1) Amendment or suspension of rules,
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved to suspend Section 2-108(h)(1) Prior
notice to public; agendas. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the request of the Director of
the Real Estate Management Division be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE SHERIFF
AGREEMENT
Transmitting a Communication from
THOMAS J. DART, Sheriff of Cook County
by
ALEXIS A. HERRERA, Budget Director
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter and execute such agreements, addenda, and
other documents as may be necessary to accomplish the County’s participation in the State’s contract with
Morrow Brothers Ford, Inc., Greenfield, Illinois, for the purchase of seventy-five (75) full size Model
Year 2008 Ford Crown Victorias.
Reason:

The Sheriff’s Office currently has an inventory of 308 vehicles with mileage in excess of
100,000. It is imperative that we begin to purchase vehicles to enable us to retire these
vehicles with excessive mileage. This purchase will help to lower overall maintenance and
gasoline costs.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $1,530,375.00. One time purchase. (717/211-549 Account). Requisition No.
82110029.
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.
The Vehicle Steering Committee concurs with this recommendation.
_________________________
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the request of the Budget Director
of the Sheriff’s Office be approved. The motion carried unanimously.
AUTHORIZATION TO ACCEPT FUNDING FROM THE
EMERGENCY TELEPHONE SYSTEM BOARD (ETSB)
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 13, 2008 from
THOMAS J. DART, Sheriff of Cook County
by
ALEXIS A. HERRERA, Budget Director
requesting authorization to accept funding from the Emergency Telephone System Board (ETSB) in the
amount of $86,028.00. This funding will accommodate the salaries and benefits of three (3) new Radio
Dispatcher/Telecommunicator positions. These positions are necessary to meet the additional
responsibilities that will be taken on by the Communications Center due to the Homeland Security
initiative that will achieve radio interoperability between the County of Cook, the City of Chicago and
Suburban Municipalities.
This funding to support these positions will come from unspent surcharge funds. The ETSB has agreed to
continue funding these positions as long as surcharge funding is available.

DEPARTMENT OF SOCIAL SERVICE
GRANT AWARD RENEWAL
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 12, 2008 from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization to renew a grant in the amount of $70,000.00 from the Illinois Criminal Justice
Information Authority (ICJIA). The funding is made available through the Federal Anti-Drug Abuse Act.
The grant will primarily fund gender-responsive treatment and aftercare services for adult female
offenders sentenced to probation or supervision for DUI-related offenses. The court’s Social Service
Department administers the programs. Outcomes for offenders will be carefully measured in compliance
with the department’s evaluation protocols.
This grant does not require an application process.
The authorization to accept the previous grant was given on October 18, 2005 by the Cook County Board
of Commissioners in the amount of $339,456.00 with a cash match of $113,152.00.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $23,333.00. Grant Award: $70,000.00. Funding period: April 1, 2008
through March 31, 2009. Funds have been appropriated in the 2008 budget in Probation and Court
Services Fee Fund, (541-818 Account), Reimbursement to Designated Fund, for this purpose.
The Budget Department has received all requisite documents, and determined the fiscal impact on Cook
County, if any.
_________________________
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the request of the Chief Judge of
the Circuit Court of Cook County be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

5702

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
OFFICE OF THE STATE'S ATTORNEY
GRANT AWARD ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication, dated February 26, 2008 from
RICHARD A. DEVINE, Cook County State’s Attorney
by
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State’s Attorney’s Office
requesting authorization to accept a no-cost extension from the U.S. Department of Justice (USDOJ),
Office of Juvenile Justice and Delinquency Prevention for the Cook County Internet Crimes Against
Children (ICAC) Task Force Program. This extension will enable the office to expend the entire award
amount as well as accomplish all of the program goals and objectives.
This grant provides funding to equip and train the Cook County ICAC Task Force partner agencies in an
effort to aggressively identify, investigate and prosecute persons who use the Internet to sexually exploit
children. The Cook County ICAC Task Force partners include representatives of the State’s Attorney’s
Office, the Chicago Police Department and law enforcement agencies from suburban Municipal Districts.
Task Force partners from local law enforcement agencies concentrate their investigative efforts in the
City of Chicago and the entire outlying suburban Cook County area.
The authorization to accept the original grant was given on July 12, 2005 by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners in the amount of $100,000.00; and authorization to accept a supplemental award was
given on November 6, 2007 in the amount of $225,000.00
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Funding period extension: April 1, 2008 through January 31, 2009.
The Budget Department has received all requisite documents, and determined the fiscal impact on Cook
County, if any.
_________________________
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the request of the Chief of the
Administrative Services Bureau of the State’s Attorney’s Office be approved. The motion carried
unanimously.
GRANT AWARD RENEWALS
Transmitting a Communication from
RICHARD A. DEVINE, Cook County State’s Attorney
by
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State’s Attorney’s Office
requesting authorization to renew a grant in the amount of $148,031.00 from the Illinois Criminal Justice
Information Authority (ICJIA), which will provide one year of funding for four (4) positions dedicated to
the Law Enforcement and Prosecutor-Based Victim Assistance Services – Juvenile Court Program.
Specifically, the grant funds three (3) delinquency courtroom specialists and one (1) transfer specialist
who work in the Victim Assistance Program at Juvenile Court.

5703

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
This grant requires the office to match 25% of the program costs. The match commitment for this
program consists of both cash and in-kind contributions. The in-kind match fully supports the salary and
fringe benefits of one (1) of the juvenile court victim specialists. The cash match consists of a portion of
the fringe benefits of the three (3) federally funded juvenile court specialists not covered by the grant
award.
This grant does not require an application process; the funding is automatically renewed.
The authorization to accept the previous grant was given on February 6, 2007 by the Cook County Board
of Commissioners in the amount of $142,338.00 with a match of $83,693.00 ($35,585.00 cash match).
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $85,287.00 [$28,009.00 - (250-818 Account); $44,978.00 - (250-110 Account);
and $12,300.00 (250-170/179 Accounts)]. Grant Award: $148,031.00. Funding period: December 19,
2007 through December 18, 2008.
Approval of this item commits Fiscal Year 2008 funds.
The Budget Department has received all requisite documents, and determined the fiscal impact on Cook
County, if any.
_________________________
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the request of the Chief of the
Administrative Services Bureau of the State’s Attorney’s Office be approved and that the Proper Officials
be authorized to sign on behalf of Cook County. The motion carried unanimously.

5708

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 9, 2008
CONTRACT RENEWAL
Transmitting a Communication from
MARIA PAPPAS, Cook County Treasurer
by
MICHAEL J. SHINE, Chief Deputy Treasurer
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew Contract No. 05-43-197 with JP Morgan
Chase Bank N.A., Chicago, Illinois, to provide lockbox, cash letter deposit and branch bank services for
the collection of property taxes for tax years 2008 through 2012.
Reason:

Since the contract was awarded on September 21, 2004 more than 3 million taxpayers have
paid property tax bills at more than 300 Chase Bank branches. Extending this contract with
no increase in costs provides a consistent payment option to the taxpayers of Cook County. A
potential conversion would not only consume significant time and resources that could be
utilized elsewhere within the Treasurer’s Office but also possibly confuse the taxpaying
public.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $400,000.00 per year, funded through compensating balances. Contract period:
February 1, 2009 through January 31, 2013.
_________________________
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to renew the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

Please be advised there will be a motion to enter into closed session, pursuant to § 2(c)(1) of the Open
Meetings Act, 5 ILCS 120/1, et seq., at the Wednesday, April 9, 2008 County Board Meeting scheduled
for 10:00 a.m. in Room 569 of the County Building, located at 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois
60602. Specifically, § 2(c)(1) of the Open Meetings Act sets forth the following:
(c) Exceptions. A public body may hold closed meetings to consider the following subjects:
(1)
The appointment, employment, compensation, discipline, performance, or dismissal of specific
employees of the public body or legal counsel for the public body, including hearing testimony on a
complaint lodged against an employee of the public body or against legal counsel for the public body to
determine its validity.
